Jamison Brereton

25 (645)
Mitra and Varun╠гa (1тАУ9, 13тАУ24) and the All Gods (10тАУ12)
Vi┼Ыvamanas Vaiya┼Ыva
24 verses: uс╣гс╣Зih, arranged in trcas ╠е
The only hymn in Maс╣Зс╕Нala VIII ostensibly devoted to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, it keeps its focus on these two gods only during the first part of the hymn (vss. 1тАУ9), which celebrates them as sovereign kings possessing the truth. Starting in verse 10 other gods join the group besought for help and protection. In particular the Sun, as a representative of the ─Аdityas, is the main subject of two tr╠еcas (vss. 16тАУ21). The final verses of the hymn (starting with vs. 19) turn their attention to the sacrificial setting. A simile concerning the ritual fire in verse 19 serves as a transition to this scene, and an address to the Sun in verse 21, which introduces the poetтАЩs тАЬbenefactors,тАЭ likewise produces a transition to the final tr╠еca (vss. 22тАУ24), a d─Бnastuti praising the gift of several horses and a chariot.
Although the thematic structure of the hymn roughly tracks the arrangement in tr╠еcas, the tr╠еcas do not have strong internal cohesion, and there is relatively little verbal unity within them.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬYou two are the protectors of the universe, divine and to be adored among the gods; therefore,(Vi┼Ыvamanas), you sacrifice to the pair who are observant of truth and endowed with real power.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

To you two, the herdsmen of all, the gods worthy of the sacrifice among the gods,
truth-possessing and of refined skill, shall I sacrifice.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For the connection of the last p─Бda of this vs. with VIII.23.30, see comm. there.

You, faithful to the Law, whose power is sanctified.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMitra and Varuс╣Зa, doers of good deeds, (diffusers of) riches, who are the charioteers (of men),well-born of old, the sons, (of Aditi), observant of vows, (you are worshipped by me).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Charioteers: or, bringers ofriches, tan─Б rathy─Б; you are worshiped: you sacrifice to them, t─Б yajase (from the previous с╣Ыca)

Jamison Brereton

They are like two charioteers along the (home) stretch (of a
racecourse), the two allies [=mitras], Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who is of strong will,
both well-born descendants from of old, whose commandments are upheld.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The du. mitr─Б╠Бis used in two different senses: on the one hand, in its appellative sense it refers to the two gods as allies; on the other mitr─Б╠Бis a pregnant dual PN, meaning тАЬMitra (and Varuс╣Зa),тАЭ with the тАЬand Varuс╣ЗaтАЭ then pleonastically+++(=redundant)+++ supplied in p─Бda b in an тАЬX and which YтАЭ construction (v├бruс╣Зo y├б┼Ы ca).

Most take t├бn─Б as another dual (to thematic t├бna-), but struggle to interpr. it. I take it as the instr. sg. of the root noun t├бn- and in this context as indicating the тАЬ(home) stretchтАЭ of a race course. The image is of two charioteers running neck and neck and therefore evenly matched.

t├бnay─Б of course echoes t├бn─Б, though it belongs to a different stem (whichever interpr. of t├бn─Б is followed). In this case I accept the general interpr. as du. to t├бnaya-.

Griffith

So, too, like charioteers are they, Mitra and sapient Varuna,
Sons high-born from of old, whose holy laws stand fast.

Geldner

Die beiden sind dauernd verb├╝ndet wie zwei Wagenrosse, Mitra und der weise Varuna, die vor alters edelgeborenen leiblichen S├╢hne, die die Gebote aufrecht halten.

Grassmann

Wie stete Wagenlenker sie, Mitra, der starke Varuna, Die sch├╢ngebornen S├╢hne wahren stets das Recht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe great and truthful Aditi, the mother (of the gods), gave birth to those two who are possessed of allaffluence, and shining with great splendour, for the (destruction of the) asuras.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Their mother, great truth-possessing Aditi, gave birth
to the two who possess all possessions, whose greatness (goes) forward to lordship.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Because the phrase asury─Б╠Аya pr├бmahas─Б is found also in VII.66.2 (also of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa), the two words must be construed together – though in both instances Geldner construes them separately (as do Renou and W. E. Hale). Moreover GeldnerтАЩs minimalist tr. of pr├бmahas- (тАЬDie тАж ErhabenenтАЭ) does not reflect its bahuvr─лhi status: it should mean something like тАШhaving their greatness forth/in frontтАЩ. In combination with the dat. asury─Б╠Аya, some forward motion seems indicated.

Griffith

These Twain, possessors of all wealth, most glorious, for supremest sway
Aditi, Mighty Mother, true to Law, brought forth.

Geldner

Die beiden Allwissenden, Erhabenen hat die gro├Яe Gesetzeshegerin, die Mutter Aditi zur Asuraw├╝rde geboren.

Grassmann

Sie, die allweisen, herrlichen, gebar zu hoher G├╢ttermacht Die grosse Mutter Aditi, die heilige.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe great Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, the two sovereign and powerful deities, the observers of truth, illumine oursolemn rite.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Powerrful: asura = impellingby being the indwelling principle, antary─Бmitay─Б prerakam;

Jamison Brereton

Great Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, sovereign kings, gods and lords [/devas and asuras],
truth-possessing, loudly sound their lofty truth.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is a particularly good passage to demonstrate that the unending rivalry between the two opposed groups Devas and Asuras so characteristic of middle Vedic literature cannot be backprojected into the core RV, since Mitra and Varuс╣Зa are called simultaneously dev─Б╠Бv ├бsur─Б.

The phrase тАШgrandson of strengthтАЩ (┼Ы├бvaso n├бp─Бt-) is used a number of times of the с╣Ъbhus (I.161.14, IV.34.6, 35.1, 8, 37.4) and only here of other divinities. It seems based on the more common ┼Ы├бvasas p├бti- (I.131.4, IV.47.3, V.6.9, etc.), with (n├б)p─Бt- echoing p├бt(i-). It also evokes semantically the phrase ┼Ы├бvasaс╕е s┼лn├║- (IV.21.1, 37.4) / putr├б- (VIII.90.2, 92.14), тАШson/child of strengthтАЩ.

The usual problem with (-)d─Бnu-: тАШgiftтАЩ or тАШdropтАЩ or both? Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(These are they) who look upon the great deities as (a bull contemplates) the herd, sovereignsobservant of truth and propitious to adoration.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The two who from lofty heaven look down upon (us) as if upon
your herds,
the truth-possessing ones were installed as sovereign kings for reverence.

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬyour herdsтАЭ of the published translation should rather be тАЬtheir herds.тАЭ

Griffith

The Twain, who from the lofty sky seem to look down on herds below,
Holy, imperial Lords, are set to be revered.

Geldner

Die vom hohen Himmel her die Gesch├╢pfe wie die Herden ├╝berschauen, die gesetzhegenden Allk├╢nige, recht f├╝r die Huldigung geschaffen.

Grassmann

Sie, die vom hohen Himmel her die Heerden gleichsam ├╝berschaun, Gerechte Herrscher zur Verehrung hingestellt,

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬObservers of truth, doers of good deeds, they sit down for the office of sovereignty; observant ofobligations, endowed with strength, they acquire vigour.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Vigour: kс╣гatriy─Б kс╣гatram ─Б┼Ыatuс╕е = balavantau balamvy─Бpnutaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Truth-possessing, strong-willed, the two took their place for sovereign kingship.
Their commandments upheld, the rulers attained their rule. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Both these verses have a subject / VP construction thatтАЩs an etymological figure: 8c тАж kс╣гatr├нy─Б kс╣гatr├бm ─Б┼Ыatuс╕е, 9c тАж nicir─Б╠Бn├н cikyatuс╕е. The latter is reinforced phonologically by the p─Бda-opening n├н cin miс╣г├бnt─Б. The unusual tmesis of preverb and participle, interrupted by the particle cid, may be (partly) accounted for by the desire to produce a ni ci- sequence matching the two that follow in that p─Бda.

Griffith

They, true to Law, exceeding strong, have sat them down for savran rule:
Princes whose laws stand fast, they have obtained their sway.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThrough knowers of the path, even before the eye (can see), causing (alll beings) to open their eyelids,existing from of old, and shining with a mild radiance, verily they have been worshipped.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The с╣Ыca is a referenceto Mitra and Varuс╣Зa as respectively presiding over day and night, ahor─Бtrayor vy─Бptena tejas─Б

Jamison Brereton

Better even than the eye at finding the way, by means of eyesight without motes,
even when blinking, the two attentive ones remain attentive. с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes
08-09 ...{Loading}...
Jamison Brereton Notes

Both these verses have a subject / VP construction thatтАЩs an etymological figure: 8c тАж kс╣гatr├нy─Б kс╣гatr├бm ─Б┼Ыatuс╕е, 9c тАж nicir─Б╠Бn├н cikyatuс╕е. The latter is reinforced phonologically by the p─Бda-opening n├н cin miс╣г├бnt─Б. The unusual tmesis of preverb and participle, interrupted by the particle cid, may be (partly) accounted for by the desire to produce a ni ci- sequence matching the two that follow in that p─Бda.

Griffith

Pathfinders even better than the eye, with unobstructed sight,
Even when they close their lids, observant, they perceive.

Geldner

Die noch besser als das Auge den Weg finden mit fehlerlosem Gesicht. Selbst wenn sie die Augen schlie├Яen, beobachten sie aufmerksam.

Grassmann

Sie, die mit unumw├╢lktem Blick mehr als das Auge Heil ersehn; Selbst wenn sie schlummern, nehmen sie beachtend wahr.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The lexeme n├н тИЪsac is found only here in the RV and indeed, judging from MonWms, in all of Sanskrit. I consider the n├н here intrusive, having crept in from passsages like VII.38.3 v├н┼Ыvebhiс╕е p─Бtu p─Бy├║bhir n├н s┼лr─л╠Бn. The lexeme n├н тИЪp─Б is fairly well attested, and so I think n├н has, as it were, hitched a ride on p─Бy├║bhiс╕е, which is ordinarily found with a form of the cognate verb as in the just cited passage.

The insistent n├нтАЩs of 11c may also have played a part.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe, injured (through his protection, offer praise) to the liberal Viс╣гс╣Зu, who harms not (his adorers); doyou who goes by thyself alone (to combat), and cause wealth to flow (to the worshipper), hear (our prayer) inbehalf of him who has commenced the sacrifice.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sindho = stotс╣Ыn prati dhan─Бn─Бm syandana┼Ы─лla viс╣гс╣Зo;

P┼лrvacittaye = pr─Бrabdhakarmaс╣Зe yajam─Бn─Бya

Jamison Brereton

Not suffering harm, we (sing) to Viс╣гс╣Зu of good drops who does not smite.
Listen, o River traveling your own course, (for us) to be first in your thought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

A verb needs to be supplied for ab to be a clause. On the basis of ┼Ыrudh├н in c, I supply тАШsingтАЩ, but any verb of service to a divinity that takes a dative would work. Geldner тАЬserveтАЭ (dienen), Renou, somewhat more elaborately тАЬapportons notre pri├иre.тАЭ Ideally we would supply sacemahi on the basis of ├бriс╣гyantaс╕е тАж sacemahi in 11c, but тИЪsac doesnтАЩt accommodate this case frame. (The few exx. with dat. given by Grassmann are to be explained otherwise.)

English translation:

тАЬYes, may he who causes the waters to flow (Parjanya), the Maruts, the A┼Ыvins, Indra, Viс╣гс╣Зu, may all(these deities) together, the showerers (of benefits, protect) that wealth for us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And that (let) the River among the waters (grant) to us, that (grant) the Maruts, that the A┼Ыvins,
and Indra and Viс╣гс╣ЗuтАФthe generous ones of one accord.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In the published translation I supply тАЬlet тАж grant,тАЭ flg. Geldner, Renou, Klein (DGRV I.403).

But I would now change that to тАЬprotect,тАЭ assuming that the t├бd + divinities in the nom. simply continues the rel. cl. in 13c mitr├│ y├бt p─Б╠Бnti тАж

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThose desirable leaders (of men), rapid in movement, break down the haughtiness of any (foe)whatever, as an impetuous current (sweeps away all obstacles).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For these superior men strike against the hostility of any zealot, like roiling (rivers) their sharp surge.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The standard interpr. take bh┼л╠Бrс╣Зayaс╕е with the frame (Geldner тАЬdiese eifrigen HerrenтАЭ), but its position at the end of the verse, far from its supposed NP, leads me to put it in the simile. (Sim. Renou) Passages like IX.17.1 тАж iva s├нndhavo, ghn├бnto vс╣Ыtr─Б╠Бс╣Зi bh┼л╠Бrс╣Зayaс╕е тАЬlike turbulent rivers тАж smashing obstaclesтАЭ give support to this assignment. The simile then consists of a nom. + acc. matching those of the frame. It might be objected that rivers donтАЩt strike against their own surge, but the image may be of fast water catching up with itself and overtopping a wave.

Because these warring Heroes stay the enmity of every foe,
As the fierce water-flood repels the furious ones.

Denn diese eifrigen Herren wehren den Anschlag eines jeden Eifers├╝chtigen ab, wie die heftige Flut.

English translation:

тАЬThis one, the lord of man (Mitra), contemplates many vast things; we follow his rites for you.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This (Sun) here, as clanlord, gazes widelyтАФthe one (gazing) over the many.
We proceed according to his commandments and yours [=─АdityasтАЩ].

Jamison Brereton Notes

itth─Б╠Бis not sufficiently represented in the published translation I would now insert тАЬjust soтАЭ after тАЬthe many.тАЭ ├бnu тАж car─Бmasi could also be subjunctive (so Geldner), тАЬwe shall proceed,тАЭ though the undoubted indicative ├бnu тАж sa┼Ыcima in the parallel phrase in 17ab supports an indicative interpr. here.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬWe observe the ancient rites of the imperial Varuс╣Зa and the renowned Mitra, (rites) that are good for(our) dwelling.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Dwelling: oky─Б = oko gс╣Ыham tasmai hit─Бni karm─Бс╣Зi

Jamison Brereton

We follow the ancient accustomed ways of the one [=the Sun] associated with the sovereign kings [=─Аdityas],
the long-heard commandments of Mitra and of Varuс╣Зa.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Flg. K├╝mmel I take the pf. of тИЪsac as presential in value.

s─Бmr─Бjy├бsya is in the same position as s─Б╠Бmr─Бjy─Бya тАШsovereign kingshipтАЩ in 8b but differently accented. The form here must be an adj. тАШrelated to sovereign kingshipтАЩ. This makes sense: its referent, the Sun, is not a sovereign king himself, but associated, as their eye and spy, with Mitra and Varuс╣Зa, who are.

The form of d─лrgha┼Ыr├║t is problematic. It appears to be a nom. sg., but the subj.

of this sentence is plural (тАЬweтАЭ). Grassmann takes it as a neut. pl. modifying vrat─Б╠Б, as do Geldner (without comment) and Renou; Scarlatta identifies it as a neut. pl. but with a query. AiG III.65-66 suggests that it follows the model of short neut. plural forms that are identical to the neut. singular belonging to other stems (type n─Б╠Бma тАШname(s)тАЩ). I think we can sympathize with the plight of a poet whoтАЩs trying to figure out how to make a neut. pl. out of a root noun ending in -t: itтАЩs simply impossible. In VII.16.8 we get ┼Ы├бrma d─лrgha┼Ыr├║t#. Since ┼Ы├бrma there could technically be plural (and there were presumbly other such expressions with neut. n-stems, etc.), itтАЩs not hard to see the poet assuming, rightly or wrongly, that -┼Ыr├║t can be a neut. pl. Oldenberg also adduces 61.2 v├нpro m├бnm─Бni d─лrgha┼Ыr├║t, where the adj. modifies nom. sg. v├нpraс╕е but could be interpr. as going with m├бnm─Бni.

Griffith

We keep the old accustomed laws, the statutes of supremacy,
The Iong-known laws of Mitra and of Varuna.

Geldner

Wir haben die alten gewohnten Gebote des Allk├╢niglichen, die weithin vernehmbaren Gebote, von Mitra und Varuna befolgt.

Grassmann

Wir sind dem alten Hausgesetz der Weltenherrschaft nachgefolgt, Der weitbekannten Ordnung Mitra-Varuna’s.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(Mitra is he) who has measured with his rays the limits of both heaven and earth; who has filled bothheaven and earth with his greatness.тАЭ

He who measured on every side the ends of heaven and of earth with his ray,
he filled both world-halves with his greatness.

I would now substitute тАШlimitsтАЩ or тАШboundariesтАЩ for тАШendsтАЩ in tr. ├бnt─Бn.

He who hath measured with his ray the boundaries of heaven and earth,

English translation:

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Jamison Brereton

This Sun held up his light under the shelter of heaven,
blazing like fire when it has been kindled and bepoured.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRaise your voice in the spacious hall of sacrifice (to him) who is lord over food derived from cattle, whois able to grant nutritious sustenance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Spacious hall: d─лrghaprasadmani: an epithet of yaj├▒e; vistс╣Ыtamsadanam yasmin yaj├▒e

Jamison Brereton

The speech at (the place) providing a long seat [=ritual ground] gains control over a prize rich in cattle;
it gains control over non-poisonous food for giving.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On d─лrgh├бprasadman-, see comm. ad VIII.10.1.

I donтАЩt quite understand тАЬnon-poisonous foodтАЭ: is this an understated way of referring to good food, or is it a real fear? In VI.39.5 we call upon the king (Indra or Soma) to give (тИЪr─Б) non-poisonous plants. I also donтАЩt understand the use of h├н here, since c does not seem to be the cause or grounds for ab, but rather a parallel clause.

Griffith

With him who sits afar the word is lord of food that comes from kine,
Controller of the gift of unempoisoned food.

Geldner

Ein Wort bei Dirghaprasadman vermag rinderreichen Lohn, es vermag ja giftlose Speise zu geben.

Grassmann

Der Weltraum hat im weiten Sitz der Erde Labung reich an Milch; Denn er vermag zu geben auch gesunden Trank.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI glorify by night and day that sun (Mitra and Varuс╣Зa) and both the heaven and earth; do you (Varuс╣Зa)ever bring us to the presence of the bountiful.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

That sun, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa: tat s┼лryam = the brightness of Mitraand Varuс╣Зa; s┼лryam suv─лryam tat varuс╣Зam maitram ca tejas

Jamison Brereton

I speak this to the Sun and to both world-halves, at evening and at dawn:
тАЬAlways rise up to us among our benefactors.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

This is presumably the speech referred to in vs. 20 that controls good things.

Griffith

So unto Surya, Heaven, and Earth at morning and at eve I speak.
Bringing enjoyments ever rise thou up for us.

Geldner

Darum bitte ich den Surya und die beiden Welten abends und morgens: Geh stets bei Gastfreien ├╝ber uns auf!

Grassmann

Die Sonne und das Weltenpaar sprech’ Abends ich und Morgens an; O gehe stets bei reicher Geber Schar uns auf.

From Uksanyayana a bay, from Harayana a white steed,
And from Susaman we obtained a hamessed car.

Ein rothbraunes und ein silberfarbenes Ross erhielten wir von dem Nachkommen des Ukschanja, dem Haraj─Бna, einen geschirrten Wagen vom Susch─Бma.

English translation:

тАЬAmong bay horses these two are pre-eminently the destroyers (of foes), and of those eager in combat;the two strong bearers of men.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These two are overflowing with (bounties) of horses, with fallow bays, for me;
and the two (horses) that carry men (are overflowing) with those that get results.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This vs. is puzzling, in part because the identity of тАЬthese twoтАЭ (t─Б╠Б) is not clear nor is the sense of nit├│┼Ыana- + GEN. The lexeme n├н тИЪtu┼Ы means тАШoverflow with, spill downтАЩ with an acc. of the largesse so spilled. See, e.g., IX.63.23 n├н to┼Ыase ray├нm “You [=Soma] spill down wealth” (cf. IV.38.1, VIII.54.8). I take the genitives here as objective gens., corresponding to the acc. in the VP. Since both ├б┼Ыvy─Бn─Бm and h├бr─лс╣З─Бс╣Г refer to horses, we might want the two that are overflowing with them to be the human (or possibly divine) givers. This is possible, if we take them as the two patrons who give horses in 22ab (and not the one who gives a chariot in 22c). Or it could be a reference to Mitra and Varuс╣Зa (so Renou). But du. nс╣Ыv─Б╠Бhas─Б тАШcarrying menтАЩ in 23c and v─Бj├нn─Бv ├бrvant─Б тАЬprize-winning chargersтАЭ in 24c must surely be horses (probably the silvery and silver horses of 22ab), and this suggests that the duals earlier in vs. 23 should have the same referent. This is GeldnerтАЩs solution, and he considers this expression shorthand for saying that the two horses given are worth as much as a whole herd of horses. This may be correct, but it is a bit difficult to wring it from the text.

kс╣Ы╠Бtvya- тАШeffective, getting resultsтАЩ is several times used of horses (VI.2.8, IX.46.1, IX.101.2), and in this context that should be the default interpr. as well.

Griffith

These two shall bring me further gain of troops of tawny-coloured steeds,
The carriers shall they be of active men of war.

English translation:

тАЬThrough this new praise (of Mitra and Varuс╣Зa) I have obtained at the same moment of the mightyprince, two fast-going sagacious steeds, with whip and reins.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Steeds: viprau = medh─Бvinam ucitau, worthy ofthe praisers of a deity

Jamison Brereton

With my newest inspired thought I have gained two altogether, along with their reins and with their whips,
two chargers great at the winning of prizes.

Jamison Brereton Notes

With Oldenberg I take v├нpr─Б as instr. sg. fem. with mat─л╠Б, contra GeldnerтАЩs voc. pl. See I.82.2.

Griffith

And the two sages have I gained who hold the reins and bear the whip,
And the two great strong coursers, with my newest song.

Geldner

Ich habe zugleich zwei herrliche sieggekr├╢nte Rennpferde nebst Z├╝gel und Peitsche f├╝r mein neuestes Gedicht als Lohn empfangen, ihr Redekundigen.

Und zwei mit Z├╝geln und Peitschen versehene sehr schnelle Renner empfing ich zugleich f├╝r mein begeistertes neustes Gedicht.
